operate after Shutdown.

3.
Section c - Description/Specifications/Work Statement
PART C - DESCRIPTION/SPECIFICATIONS
STATEMENT OF WORK (SOW)
ANNUAL PREVENTATIVE MAINTENANCE - FIRE SUPPRESSION AND FIRE ALARM SYSTEMS
U.S. GOVERNMENT PUBLISHING OFFICE
1.0. GENERAL INFORMATION
1.1. Project Title
Annual Preventive Maintenance (PM) Services - Fire Suppression and Fire Alarm Systems.
1.2. Contract Type
Firm-Fixed-Price (FFP) Service Contract.
1.3. Period of Performance
Base Year: One (1) year.
Option Years: Three (3) one-year options.
Total Contract Duration: Up to four (4) years.
Option years may be exercised at the sole direction of the Government..
1.4. Location
The United States Government Publishing Office (GPO) is located at 732 North Capitol Street NW, Washington, DC
20401. The office produces and distributes information products and services for all three
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 7 of 35
branches of the Federal Government, including U.S. passports for the Department of State as well as the official
publications of Congress, the White House, and other Federal agencies in digital and print formats.
The existing fire suppression and fire alarm systems of the four GPO Buildings (A, B, C, D) total a gross floor area of
1,419,507 square feet. A building list and system inventory from the 2024 Annual PM Report will be provided as
Government-Furnished Information (GFI).
2.0. PROJECT OVERVIEW AND OBJECTIVES
The objective of this contract is to provide systematic, code-compliant preventive maintenance, inspection, and testing of fire
alarm and fire suppression systems to ensure:
Continuous life safety system operability.
Compliance with applicable codes and GPO standards.
Early identification of system deficiencies.
Accurate and complete system documentation.
3.0. SCOPE OF WORK
3.1. General Requirements
The Contractor shall furnish all labor, supervision, tools, equipment, materials, documentation, and coordination
necessary to perform annual preventive maintenance services for the fire alarm and fire suppression systems in
accordance with this Statement of Work.
3.2. Systems Included
Services shall include inspection, testing, and reporting for the following systems, where present:
Fire Suppression Systems:
Wet-pipe sprinkler systems
Dry-pipe and pre-action sprinkler systems.
Standpipe systems.
Fire pumps.
Control valves, supervisory devices, gauges, and alarms.
Fire Alarm Systems:
The buildings utilize EST3 systems manufactured by Edwards.
Fire alarm control panels (FACP).
Networked panels and remote annunciators.
Initiating devices (smoke, heat, duct detectors, manual pull stations).
Notification appliances (horns, strobes, speakers).
Power supplies, batteries, and circuit supervision.
Monitoring and communication interfaces.
3.3. Exclusions
The following are excluded from this contract unless separately authorized in writing by the Contracting Officer:
Corrective repairs or system modifications.
Replacement of failed components.
System upgrades or code retrofit work.
Emergency response services.
4.0. APPLICABLE CODES, STANDARDS, AND CRITERIA
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 8 of 35
All services shall be performed in accordance with the latest adopted editions of the following:
Manufacturer requirements for EST3.
NFPA 13 - Installation of Sprinkler Systems (reference).
NFPA 14 - Installation of Standpipe Systems (reference).
NFPA 20 - Installation of Stationary Pumps for Fire Protection.
NFPA 25 - Inspection, Testing and Maintenance of Water Based Fire Protection Systems.
NFPA 72 - National Fire Alarm and Signaling Code.
GPO Design Standards and Life Safety Requirements.
OSHA regulations and applicable Authority Having Jurisdiction (AHJ) requirements.
5.0. TECHNICAL REQUIREMENTS
5.1. Fire Suppression Annual Preventive Maintenance
The Contractor shall perform inspections and testing in accordance with NFPA 25, including at a minimum:

Components Corrected After Deficiency Repair: The Contractor shall retest devices or circuits repaired or replaced by
Government personnel to verify proper operation. Retesting shall be limited to affected components. All retests will be
requested from the COR to the Contractor, and will be priced under a separate, Not to Exceed (NTE) Contract Line-Item
Number (CLIN). The contractor shall respond to any retest requests within fourteen (14) calendar days.
5.2.
Fire Alarm Annual Preventive Maintenance
The Contractor shall perform inspections and testing as required by NFPA 72 and EST3 manufacturer requirements,
including at a minimum:
FIRE ALARM INSPECTION AND TESTING REQUIREMENTS:
DEVICE
ANNUAL
Smoke detectors
TEST
Heat detectors
TEST
Pull stations
TEST
Duct smoke detectors
TEST
Waterflow switch
TEST
Dry pipe valves
TEST
Hi/Lo pressure switch
TEST
Tamper switch
TEST
Strobes/horns
TEST
Smoke detectors:
All detectors shall be tested with a listed spray test smoke.
All detectors shall be tested in all areas accessible to the Contractor.
A validation of all building interfaces shall be noted on the test report (HVAC shut-down, elevator recall,
etc.).
Heat detectors:
All restorable heat detectors shall be tested utilizing a heat gun (on low setting) or a hair dryer.
Validation of all building interfaces shall be noted on test report (HVAC shut-down, elevator recall, etc.).
Non-restorable heat detectors SHALL NOT be tested using a heat source.
Pull stations:
All pull stations shall be tested and re-set.
Validation of all building interfaces shall be noted on test report (HVAC shut-down, elevator recall, etc.).
Duct smoke detectors: Provide testing as required by NFPA 72.
Waterflow switch: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25.
Dry pipe valves: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25.
Hi/Lo pressure switch: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25.
Tamper switch: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25. Switch shall give immediate activation of supervisory
signal at the fire alarm panel.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 10 of 35
Strobes/horns: Provide testing as required by NFPA 72.
Tamper switch (for buildings equipped with sprinklers only): Each system valve tamper switch shall be tested by partially
closing the valve to initiate a tamper signal, locking in the nearby monitor module.
Dry Valves (for buildings equipped with sprinklers only): Test pressure switch using the inspectors test located on valve.
Alarm Devices:
All sprinkler alarm devices shall be serviced per the table. Verify alarm panel device description/location
for accuracy.
All sprinkler flow initiation devices shall alarm within 90 seconds.
System Checks:
No visible water leaks or standing water (clogged drains).
Record all test data, static pressures, residual pressures
Fire pump test shall not activate general alarm (denotes system pressure problems).
During weekly pump runs: verify fire pump and jockey pump start and stop pressures.
Jockey pump stop pressure shall be equal to or higher than fire pump churn (zero flow) pressure. Jockey
pump run cycles should be no more than 10 runs within a 24hr period.
Dry Sprinkler Valves:
All systems shall be drained for a minimum of 4 hours following a valve trip test.
Inspect for excessive compressor run.
Check for proper system air pressure per manufacturer's cut sheet.
Devices Corrected After Deficiency Repair: The Contractor shall retest devices or circuits repaired or replaced by
Government personnel to verify proper operation. Retesting shall be limited to affected components.
6.0. SERVICE EXECUTION
6.1. Scheduling and Coordination
All work shall be coordinated with the GPO Contracting Officer's Representative (COR).
Services shall be performed during normal business hours unless otherwise approved.
Work shall be sequenced to minimized system downtime and occupant disruption.
6.2. System Impairments
All impairments shall be coordinated and approved in advance.
Systems shall be fully restored to normal operation prior to Contractor demobilization.
7.0. SUBMITTALS AND DELIVERABLES
7.1. Required Deliverables
For each building serviced, the Contractor shall submit:
Annual inspection and testing reports.
Device counts and test results.
Deficiency reports identifying:
Code deficiencies.
Non-code performance deficiencies.
Observed system conditions.
System status summary at completion.
Retest documentation for devices or components retested following completion of deficiency repairs,
including pass/fail results and confirmation of system operation status.
7.2. Submittal Format and Timing
Reports shall be submitted electronically in PDF format.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 11 of 35
Deliverables shall be submitted within ten (10) business days of service completion for each building.
8.0. QUALITY ASSURANCE / QUALITY CONTROL (QA/QC)
The Contractor shall maintain a Quality Control Plan (QCP).
All work shall be performed by qualified, trained and properly certified technicians.
Fire Pump Representative/Technician:
Minimum of five (5) years of relevant work experience; and Qualified and fire pump certified by
the fire pump manufacturer for the fire pump identified.
Sprinkler Technician:
Qualified to perform NFPA 25 inspection and testing.
Minimum of five (5) years of relevant work experience; and NICET Inspection, Testing and
Maintenance certified at Level Il or higher.
Fire Alarm Technician:
Qualified and experienced in accordance with Section 4.3.3. of NFPA 72, National Fire Alarm
Code, and NICET-certified at Level II or higher.
Minimum of five (5) years of experience servicing addressable fire alarm systems.
Experience inspecting systems comparable in size/complexity to the Government's EST3
systems.
No programming changes without Contracting Officer authorization.
The Government may witness inspections and testing at its discretion.
9.0. SAFETY AND SECURITY
The Contractor shall comply with all OSHA, GPO safety, and building security requirements.
Personnel shall meet all badging and escort requirements.
Work areas shall be always maintained in a safe and orderly condition.
10.0.
ACCEPTANCE AND VERIFICATION
Acceptance is contingent upon:
Completion of all required preventive maintenance tasks.
Restoration of systems to normal operational status.
Submission and Government acceptance of required documentation.
Incomplete or deficient work shall be corrected at no additional cost to the Government.
Completion of required retesting following correction of identified deficiencies, where applicable, and submission
of corresponding retest documentation.
11.0.
PROJECT MANAGEMENT AND COMMUNICATION
The Contractor shall designate a Project Manager as the single point of contact.
Project Manager Qualifications:
Minimum five (5) years of experience managing fire alarm and suppression service contracts.
Experience managing multi-building facilities.
Familiarity with addressable fire alarm systems comparable to the Government's EST3 systems.
Demonstrated knowledge of NFPA 72 and NFPA 25.
Issues affecting life safety or system operability shall be reported immediately to the COR.
Coordination meetings shall be conducted as required.
12.0.
CLOSEOUT
At the conclusion of the Base Year and each Option Year, the Contractor shall provide:
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 12 of 35
Final inspection and deficiency summary.
Confirmation of system operational status.
All outstanding documentation prior to final payment.
13.0.
AGENCY OPERATIONS INFORMATION
13.1.
Hours of Service
The Contractor shall perform services during normal GPO business hours unless otherwise directed by the
Contracting Officer or Contracting Officer's Representative (COR).
Normal Business Hours:
Monday through Friday, 7:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m.
After-Hours Work:
Certain tasks may require performance outside normal business hours, including evenings, weekends, or
Federal holidays, to support GPO operations, emergency response, or to minimize disruption to occupants.
After-hours work shall be coordinated in advance with the COR.
No overtime, premium pay, or schedule changes shall be authorized unless approved in advance by the COR.
13.2.
Identification Badges and Security Access
All Contractor personnel requiring access to GPO facilities must comply with GPO security and badging requirements.
Contractor personnel shall obtain and visibly display GPO-issued identification badges at all times while on GPO
property. GPO will provide affiliated badges with security background checks to the Contractor, allowing them to
escort their workers onto the premises. If a Contractor has not been granted an affiliated badge, they must exchange
a valid federal or state-issued identification for a GPO Visitor's badge to enter the premises. Identification badges are
property of GPO and must be returned immediately upon contract completion, personnel reassignment, or
termination. Contractor personnel may be denied access or have badges revoked for failure to comply with security
policies or conduct standards.
13.3.
Sign-In I Sign-Out Requirements
All Contractor personnel are required to sign-in at 732 North Capitol St. NE Washington, DC 22041. All Contractor
personnel are required to sign-out at the same location above.
13.4.
Parking and Transportation
Parking within the GPO complex is extremely limited and not guaranteed. It is the responsibility of Contractor
personnel to purchase a parking pass for the designated parking areas. GPO will not validate or make reimbursement
for parking violations of the Contractor's personnel under any circumstances. Unauthorized parking on GPO property
may result in citation, towing or revocation of site access privileges.
13.5.
Conduct and Compliance
Contractor personnel shall conduct themselves in a professional manner consistent with the operational environment
of a Federal legislative complex. Smoking, tobacco use, or e-cigarettes are prohibited inside all GPO buildings. No
individual is permitted to bring illegal drugs, alcohol or firearms of any type onto a government installation. Disruptive
behavior, failure to follow access procedures, or noncompliance with GPO rules may result in removal from the site
and replacement at no additional cost to the Government.
13.6.
Contractor Responsibility
The Contractor shall be responsible all facilities in which the work will take place and to also be familiar with the
conditions under which the work will be accomplished. The Contractor shall inspect existing conditions prior to
commencing work, including elements subject to damage or movement during the project. The Contractor shall
provide adequate personnel to reset alarm panels. Should the work create dust, water or mud, the Contractor shall be
responsible for cleaning the floors and walls. The Contractor shall be responsible for the removal and replacement of
all ceiling tiles affected by the work.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 13 of 35
13.7.
Tagging Requirements
The Contractor shall notify the COR/ACOR if panel alarm activation occurs unexpectedly during inspection, testing
and immediately upon occurrence. The Contractor shall contact the COR/ACOR for procedures to take monitoring
systems offline during their procedures. The Contractor shall take all efforts to prevent this from occurring with any
regularity.
A panel must show a "no fault or no trouble" condition upon completion of test. After the tests and inspections are
completed, the Contractor shall contact the COR prior to placing monitoring systems back online, and the appropriate
tags will be attached indicating the system status. The Contractor shall be responsible for any damage to the fire
system during the work processes. If applicable, the tagging and labeling system must clearly identify either a "blue"
(operational condition) or "yellow" (troubled condition but functional) or "red" (Impaired or Fault but functional) or "red"
(System Inoperable). This labeling system applies to all circuit boards, components in the control panels, annunciator
panels, transponders, printers, keyboards, monitors, and peripheral devices (smoke detectors, pull stations, audible
and visible units, door contacts, tampers, flows, etc.) associated with the fire alarm/sprinkler system.
(End of Section C)

the works described in Section J Attachments. The Contractor is responsible for inspection of its own work to ensure that
all work performed conforms to the terms and conditions of the contract.

option year. Exact dates will be outlined in the resulting contract.
For work to be performed at the government site, the Contractor must establish a standard holiday schedule that exactly
coincides with the Government's schedule for holidays. The Contractor is responsible for tracking the official Federal
Holidays for any given calendar year. Holidays and other non-workdays are not billable unless work is specifically
requested by the government and productive hours are performed on those days.

CONTRACTING OFFICER S AUTHORITY
The Contracting Officer is the only person authorized to make or approve any changes in any of
the requirements of this contract and notwithstanding any provisions contained elsewhere in this
contract, the said authority remains solely the Contracting Officer S. In the event the Contractor makes
any changes at the direction of any person other than the Contracting Officer, the change will
be considered to have been made at the contractor S risk. No adjustment will be made to the contract
terms and conditions of this contract, including price.
CONTRACTING OFFICER S REPRESENTATIVE (COR)
The COR is responsible for the technical aspects of the project and serves as technical liaison with the
Contractor.
The COR is also responsible for the final inspection and acceptance of all products, services, reports, and
such other responsibilities as may be specified in this contract. The COR is not authorized to make any
commitments or otherwise obligate the GPO or authorize any changes, which affect the Contract price,
terms or conditions. Any Contractor request for changes shall be referred to the Contracting Officer directly
or through the COR. No such changes shall be made without the expressed prior authorization of the
Contracting Officer.
If the Contractor performs a service that alters the current cost, quantity, or scope without prior written
approval from the CO, the Contractor does so at his/her own risk. The COR may designate assistant
COR(s) to act for the COR by naming such assistant(s) in writing and transmitting a copy of such
designation through the Contracting Officer to the Contractor.
The COR is not authorized to make any commitments or otherwise obligate the GPO or authorize any
changes, which affect the quantity, quality, scope or Contract price. All requests for changes shall be
referred to the Contracting Officer directly or through the COR. No such changes shall be made
without the expressed prior authorization of the Contracting Officer. If the Contractor performs a
service that alters the current cost, quantity, or scope without prior written approval from the CO, the
Contractor does so at his/her own risk. The COR may designate an alternate COR(s) to act for the
COR by naming such alternate(s) in writing and transmitting a copy of such designation through the
Contracting Officer to the Contractor.

MERGERS, ACQUISITIONS, NOVATIONS, AND CHANGE-OF-NAME AGREEMENTS
In accordance with MMAR 42.12, if a contractor merges, is acquired, or recognizes a successor in
interest to Government contracts when contractor assets are transferred; or, recognizes a change in a
contractor's name; or, executes novation agreements and change-of-name agreements, the
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 17 of 35
contractor shall notify the CO and provide a copy of the novation or other any other agreement that
changes the status of the contractor.
Title 41 U.S.C. 6305 prohibits the transfer of Government contracts from an awardee to a third party.
However, the Government may, when in its interest, novate an awardee's contract to a third party when
there is a transfer of all of the awardee's assets or the entire portion of the assets involved in the performance
of the contract.
For a novation to be approved by the CO, the following elements shall occur:
The company shall submit a novation agreement with all the required legal elements in accordance with
MMAR 42.12.
The novation agreement shall include the transfer of personnel performing work under the contract and any
awarded delivery orders, as applicable.
The novation agreement shall be determined by the CO to be in the best interest of the Government.
8. Section H - Special Contract Requirements
H.1 KEY PERSONNEL
Certain experienced professionals and/or technical personnel are essential for successful accomplishment of the work to
be performed under this contract. Such personnel are defined as "Key Personnel" and are those persons whose resumes
were submitted for evaluation of the proposal. The contractor agrees that such personnel shall not be removed from the
contract or replaced without compliance with the following:
a. The personnel specified under this contract are essential to the work the contractor agrees to perform hereunder
be essential to the work. The contractor agrees that personnel may not be removed from the contract work or
replaced without compliance with paragraphs (b) and (c) of this section.
b. If one or more of the key personnel, for whatever reason, becomes, or is expected to become, unavailable for
work under this contract for a continuous period exceeding 30 work days, or is expected to devote substantially
less effort to the work than indicated in the proposal or initially anticipated, the contractor shall immediately notify
the Contracting Officer and shall, subject to the concurrence of the contracting officer, promptly replace the
personnel with personnel of at least substantially equal ability and qualifications. Personnel must be replaced
within 30 days of the contractor departing the contract. This substitution must be pre-vetted and able to pass
through our background check by our Security Services unit. The incumbent must be able to obtain a public trust
clearance.
c. Each request for approval of substitutions must be in writing and contain a detailed explanation of the
circumstances necessitating the proposed substitutions. The request must also contain a complete resume for
the proposed substitute and other information requested or needed by the contracting officer to evaluate the
proposed substitution. The Contracting Officer and the Contracting Officer's Representative shall evaluate the
contractor's request, and the contracting officer shall promptly notify the contractor of his or her decision in
writing.
d. If the Contracting Officer determines that suitable and timely replacement of key personnel who have been
reassigned, terminated, or have otherwise become unavailable for the contract work is not reasonably
forthcoming, or that the resultant reduction of productive effort would be so substantial as to impair the
successful completion of the contract or the service order, the contract may be terminated by the contracting
officer for default or for the convenience of the Government, as appropriate. If the Contracting Officer finds the
contractor at fault for the condition, the contract price or profit/fixed fee may be equitably adjusted downward to
compensate the Government for any resultant delay, loss, or damage.

H.2 CONTRACTOR'S EMPLOYEES IDENTIFICATION AND GOVERNMENT CONTRACTOR RELATIONS
a. All contractor personnel when attending meetings, sending emails, or participating on telephone calls shall
identify themselves as contractor personnel. Identification in meetings and on Microsoft Teams shall be at the
beginning of the call or meeting to allow government personnel to excuse contractors if appropriate.
b. Contractor personnel shall identify themselves with their company name in the signature block of emails.
C. Pursuant to MMAR 7.5, the contractor shall not perform any inherently governmental actions under this contract.
No contractor employee shall hold him or herself out to be a government employee, agent, or representative. No
contractor employee shall state orally or in writing at any time that he or she is acting on behalf of the
Government. No Employer-employee relationship exists of will exist under this Contract. Contractor's employees
shall not:
i. Be placed in a position where they are under the supervision, direction, or evaluation of a government
employee.
ii. Be placed in a position of command, supervision, administration or control over Government personnel,
or over personnel of other contractors under other GPO's contracts or become a part of the Government
organization.
iii. Be used in administration or supervision of Government procurement activities.
d. d. The services to be performed under this contract do not require the contractor of his employees to exercise
personal judgment and discretion on behalf of the Government. Rather, contractor personnel will act and
exercise personal judgment and discretion on behalf of the contractor.
H.3 INSURANCE
Neither GPO nor the US Government shall in any event be liable or responsible for any damage or injury to any person or
property occasioned by the actions of the Contractor or Contractor's employees in performing under this contract. The
Contractor must maintain adequate insurance with the proper coverage limits, including general liability and professional
liability insurances, and others if needed, during the term of this contract, insuring the contractor against any claims for
injury or damage.
H.4 DISSEMINATIONOF INFORMATION
There shall be no dissemination or publication, except within and between the Contractor and any Subcontractors, of
information developed under this contract or contained in the reports to be furnished pursuant to this contract without prior
written approval of the Contracting Officer and Contracting Officer's Representative(s). Language similar to this provision
shall be included in all
subcontracts to this contract. This provision includes news releases: blogs, posts, and published papers.
H.5 NOTIFICATION OF DEBARMENT/SUSPENSION STATUS
The Contractor shall provide written notice to the Contracting Officer within ten (10) calendar days of being suspended,
debarred, or declared ineligible by any Department or other Federal Agency, or upon receipt of a notice of proposed
debarment during the performance of this contract.

H.8 CONFLICTS OF INTEREST
a. It is understood and agreed that some of the work required hereunder may place the Contractor, or
its personnel or its subcontractors or their personnel (hereinafter referred to collectively as
Contractor), in the position of having a potential personal or organizational conflict of interest (OCI),
i.e., because of other activities or relationships with other persons, (1) the Contractor is unable or
potentially unable to
render impartial assistance or advice; or (2) the Contractor objectivity in performing the Contract is or
might be impaired; or (3) the Contractor may receive an unfair competitive advantage; or (4) the
Contractor may have a financial or other personal interest which would or potentially would impair
his/her objectivity and/or from which he/she would improperly benefit. Further discussion of OCIs
may be found in MMAR 9.5. The performance/actions of personnel under this Contract will be
imputed to the Contractor (or subcontractor) by whom they are employed or retained, and the
performance/actions of any subcontractor will be imputed to the Contractor, unless the Contractor,
on a case-by-case basis, can demonstrate otherwise and satisfy the Contracting Officer that such
imputation is unreasonable.
b. If it is discovered that the Contractor engaged in any activities which constitute a potential or actual
conflict without having first obtained the Contracting Officer S approval to undertake such activities;
or if it is subsequently discovered that, notwithstanding the Contracting Officer S authorization to
undertake the activity based on his/her initial determination that no significant potential conflict
existed or appeared to exist, a conflict did, in fact exist or arise, restrictions, as permitted by MMAR
9.5, on the Contractor future activities may be placed unilaterally by the Contracting Officer for this
contract or the Contracting Officer for such other contract as may be involved in the conflict, and
other remedies (including termination of this contract for default, debarment or suspension, and
those permitted by the clauses of this contract entitled Cancellation, Rescission and Recovery of
Funds for Illegal or Improper Activity (MMAR 52.203 8) and Price or Fee Adjustment for Illegal or
Improper Activity [MMAR 52.203 10]), may be taken by GPO.
H.9 RESTRICTIONSAGAINST DISCLOSURE
The Contractor agrees, in the performance of this contract, to keep the information furnished by the Government
or acquired/developed by the Contractor in performance of the contract and designated by the Contracting
Officer or Contracting Officer S Representative, in the strictest confidence. The Contractor also agrees not to
publish or otherwise divulge such information, in whole or in part, in any manner or form, nor to authorize or
permit others to do so, taking such reasonable measures as are necessary to restrict access to such information
while in the Contractor's possession, to those employees needing such information to perform the work
described herein, i.e., on a need to know basis. The Contractor agrees to immediately notify the Contracting
Officer in writing in the event that the Contractor determines or has reason to suspect a breach of this
requirement has occurred.
All Contractor staff working on any of the described tasks may, at Government request, be required to sign formal non-
disclosure and/or conflict of interest agreements to guarantee the protection and integrity of Government information and
documents.
The Contractor shall insert the substance of this special contract requirement, including this paragraph (c), in all
subcontracts when requiring a restriction on the release of information developed or obtained in connection with the
performance of the contract.
H.10 PROTECTIONOF PROPERTY
Contractor Responsibility. If due to the default, negligence (whether of action or omission) and/or dishonesty of
040ADV-26-R-0021

the Contractor or its employees, any Government-owned or controlled property is lost or damaged as a result of

at its own expense, all property lost or damaged. The Contractor shall protect materials in his custody against the
transportation, fire, theft, weather, and other hazards avoidance in the exercise of the "highest degree of care."
H.11 STANDARDS OF CONDUCT
(a)
When the Contractor is onsite at a federal building, the Contractor shall be responsible for
maintaining satisfactory standards of employee competency, conduct, appearance, and integrity.
Each employee or supervisor of the Contractor is expected to adhere to the rules associated with
that federal building, and to adhere to standards of behavior that reflect credit on themselves, their
employer, and the Federal Government.
(b)
The Contractor shall be responsible for taking such disciplinary action, including suspension without pay or
removal from the worksite, with respect to its employees, as may be necessary to enforce those standards.
(c)
Where applicable, the requirements of this clause shall be expressly incorporated into
subcontract(s) and shall be applicable to all Sub-Contractor employees who may perform
services or work at the federal building and grounds of this contract.
H.12 COOPERATIONWITH OTHER ON-SITE CONTRACTORS
When the Government undertakes or awards other contracts for additional work at the facilities, the
Contractor shall:
(a) Fully cooperate with the other Contractors and Government employees, and
(b) Carefully fit its own work to such other additional contracted work as may be directed by the
Contracting Officer's Representative (COR). The Contractor shall not commit or permit any act
which shall interfere with the performance of work awarded to another Contractor or with the
performance of other Government employees.
(c) In any case where, in the course of fulfilling the contract requirements, the Contractor disturbs
any work guaranteed under another separate contract, the Contractor shall restore such
disturbed work to a condition satisfactory to the COR and guarantee such restored work to the
same extent as it was guaranteed under the applicable other contract.
H.13 WORK ON A GOVERNMENT INSTALLATION
In performing onsite work under this contract on a Government installation or in a Government building, the
Contractor shall:
(a) Conform to the specific safety requirements established by the contract.
(b) Comply with the safety rules of the Government installation that concern related activities not
directly addressed in this contract.
(c) Take all reasonable steps and precautions to prevent accidents and preserve the life and health
of Contractor and Government personnel connected in any way with performance under this
contract.
(d) Take such additional immediate precautions as the Contracting Officer or Contracting Officer's
Representative (COR) may reasonably require for safety and accident prevention purposes.
(e) Conform to all required security requirements.
H.14 CONTRACTOR ACCESS AND SECURITY REQUIREMENTS FOR THIS CONTRACT
The performance of this contract requires employees of the prime contractor or its subcontractors, affiliates,
consultants, or team members ("contractor employees") to have access to and to the extent authorized,
mobility within, a GPO facility. GPO may close and or otherwise deny contractor employees access to a
GPO facility for a portion of a business day or longer for various reasons including, but not limited, to the
following events:
(a) Federal public holidays for Federal employees in accordance with 5 U.S.C. 6103; Fires, floods,
earthquakes, and unusually severe weather, including but not limited to snowstorms, tornadoes,
and hurricanes; Occupational safety or health hazards; Lapse in Appropriations; or Federal
Statute, Executive Order, Presidential Proclamation, or any other unforeseen reason. In such
events, the contractor employees may be denied access to a GPO facility that is ordinarily
available for the contractor to perform work or make delivery, as required by the contract.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 21 of 35
In all instances where contractors are denied access or required to vacate a GPO facility, in part
or in whole, the contractor shall be responsible to ensure contractor personnel working under the
contract comply. If the circumstances permit, the contracting officer will provide direction to the
contractor, either directly or through the Contracting Officer's Representative (COR), which could
include continuing on-site performance during the GPO facility closure period; however, if
Government
oversight is required and is not available, on-site performance shall not be allowed. In the
absence of such direction, the contractor shall exercise sound judgment to minimize unnecessary
contract costs and performance impacts, for example, performing required work off- site if
possible or reassigning personnel to other activities if appropriate.
The contractor shall be responsible for monitoring the Office of Personnel Management at opm.gov, the
local radio, television stations, GPO web sites, and other communication channels. Once the facility is
accessible, the contractor shall resume contract performance as required by the contract.
For the period that GPO facilities were not accessible to contractors who required access in order to perform
the services, the contracting officer may-
Adjust the contract performance or delivery schedule for a period equivalent to the period the GPO facility
was not accessible; Forego the work; or Reschedule the work by mutual agreement of the parties.
Notification procedures of a GPO facility closure, including contractor denial of access, are as follows:
The contractor shall be responsible for notification of its employees of the GPO facility closure to include
denial of access to the GPO facility. The dismissal of GPO employees in accordance with statute and
regulations providing for such dismissals shall not, in itself, equate to a GPO facility closure in which
contractors are denied access. Moreover, the leave status of GPO employees shall not be conveyed or
imputed to contractor personnel.
Accordingly, unless the GPO facility is closed and the contractor is denied access to the facility, the
contractor shall continue performance in accordance with the contract.
(a) Access to Government facilities and resources, including equipment and systems, will be limited
and personnel necessary to administer contract performance may not be available. Generally,
supply and service contracts that are funded beyond the date of the lapse in appropriation and
do not require access to Government facilities, active administration by Government personnel
or the use of Government resources in a manner that would cause the Government to incur
additional obligations during the lapse in appropriation may continue. If a delivery date for a
contract falls during the period of a lapse in appropriations, Government personnel may not be
available to receive delivery.
(b) Contractors are directed to consult with a contracting officer before attempting to make a
delivery. Contracting officers will be available throughout the lapse in appropriation period to
provide guidance. Once OMB guidance is given, CORs, in consultation with the contracting
officer, will notify those contractors that are deemed by the Program Office to be performing
excepted work and identify the contractor personnel requiring access to GPO facilities. CORs
will also coordinate directly with facility management or physical security personnel at respective
locations to ensure that the names of contractor personnel requiring access to Government
facilities during the lapse in appropriations are provided to physical security personnel.
(c) Contractors who are not designated as performing excepted work are not allowed access to
Government facilities or to utilize Government resources in a manner that would incur any
additional obligation of funding on behalf of the Government during the lapse in appropriation.
(d) All contractors working on this contract must undergo fingerprinting and background checks.
This includes all subcontractors.
(e) All contractors will be required to pass through metal detectors and all backpacks,
toolboxes/bags, lunch boxes etc. will be subject to inspection.
(f) All contractors will be required to exchange their government approved ID badge for a contractor
access badge at the beginning of their work shift. Contractors will not be allowed to leave the
building with their access badges under any circumstances. Contractors will exchange their
access badges for their personal ID's at the end of their workday or any time a contractor leaves
the building.

DISPUTES (GPO Clause June 2008)
a. This contract is subject to the Contract Disputes Act of 1978, as amended (41 U.S.C. 601-613, and as modified by Section
1501 of Title I of Division H of the Consolidated Appropriations Act, 2008, Public Law No. 110-161).
b. Except as provided in the Act, all disputes arising under or relating to this contract shall be resolved under this clause.
"Claim,"; as used in this clause, means a written demand or written assertion by one of the contracting parties seeking, as
a matter of right, the payment of money in a sum certain, the adjustment or interpretation of contract terms, or other relief arising
under or relating to this contract. However, a written demand or written assertion by the Contractor seeking the payment of
money exceeding $50,000 is not a claim under the Act until certified. A voucher, invoice, or other routine request for payment
that is not in dispute when submitted is not a claim under the Act. The submission may be converted to a claim under the Act, by
complying with the submission and certification requirements of this clause, if it is disputed either as to liability or amount or is not
acted upon in a reasonable time.
(1) A claim by the Contractor shall be made in writing and, unless otherwise stated in this contract, submitted within 6 years after
accrual of the claim to the Contracting Officer for a written decision. A claim by the Government against the Contractor shall be
subject to a written decision by the Contracting Officer.
(2)(i) The Contractor shall provide the certification specified in paragraph (d)(2)(iii) of this clause when submitting any claim
exceeding $50,000.
i. The certification requirement does not apply to issues in controversy that have not been submitted as all or part
of a claim.
ii. The certification shall state as follows: "I certify that the claim is made in good faith; that the supporting data are
accurate and complete to the best of my knowledge and belief; that the amount requested accurately reflects the
contract adjustment for which the Contractor believes the Government is liable; and that I am duly authorized to
certify the claim on behalf of the Contractor;
(3) The certification may be executed by any person duly authorized to bind the Contractor with respect to the claim.
e. For Contractor claims of $50,000 or less, the Contracting Officer must, if requested in writing by the Contractor,
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 25 of 35
f.
render a decision within 60 days of the request. For Contractor-certified claims over $50,000, the Contracting
Officer must, within 60 days, decide the claim or notify the Contractor of the date by which the decision will be
made.
g. The Contracting Officer's decision shall be final unless the Contractor appeals, within ninety (90) days of receipt of
a Contracting Officer's decision, to the U.S. Government Accountability Office Contract Appeals Board (GAO CAB),
441 G Street, NW, Room 7182, Washington, DC, 20548; Facsimile: 202-512-9749; E-Mail: CAB@gao.gov.
h. If the claim by the Contractor is submitted to the Contracting Officer or a claim by the Government is presented to
the Contractor, the parties, by mutual consent, may agree to use alternative dispute resolution (ADR). If the
Contractor refuses an offer for ADR, the Contractor shall inform the Contracting Officer, in writing, of the
Contractor's specific reasons for rejecting the offer.
i.
The Government shall pay interest on the amount found due and unpaid from (1) the date that the Contracting
Officer receives the claim (certified, if required); or (2) the date that payment otherwise would be due, if that date is
later, until the date of payment. With regard to claims having defective certifications, interest shall be paid from the
date that the Contracting Officer initially receives the claim. [A defective certification means a certificate which alters
or otherwise deviates from the language in(d)(2)(iii) above, or which is not executed by a person duly authorized to
bind the contractor with respect to the claim. Failure to certify shall not be deemed to be a defective certification.]
Simple interest on claims shall be paid at the rate, fixed by the Secretary of the Treasury as provided in the Act,
which is applicable to the period during which the Contracting Officer receives the claim and then at the rate
applicable for each 6- month period as fixed by the Treasury Secretary during the pendency of the claim.
j.
The Contractor shall proceed diligently with performance of this contract, pending final resolution of any request for
relief, claim, appeal, or action arising under the contract, and comply with any decision of the Contracting Officer.
k. This contract clause, Disputes (GPO Clause June 2008), cancels and supersedes the contract clause, MMAR
Dispute 52.233-1 (July 2002), and all other references to the contract clause, Disputes. This contract clause also
cancels and supersedes any other disputes language currently included in existing contractual actions.
(End of Clause)

MMAR 52.217-8 OPTION TO EXTEND SERVICES (NOV 1999)
The Government may require continued performance of any services within the limits and at the rates specified
in the contract. These rates may be adjusted only as a result of revisions to prevailing labor rates provided by
the Secretary of Labor. The option provision may be exercised more than once, but the total extension of
performance hereunder shall not exceed 6 months. The Contracting Officer may exercise the option by written
notice to the Contractor within 30 days.
(End of clause)
MMAR 52.217-9 Option to Extend the Term of the Contract (Mar 2000)
The Government may extend the term of this contract by written notice to the Contractor within 30 days; provided that the
Government gives the Contractor a preliminary written notice of its intent to extend at least 30 days before the contract
expires. The preliminary notice does not commit the Government to an extension.
If the Government exercises this option, the extended contract shall be considered to include this option clause.
The total duration of this contract, including the exercising of any options under this clause, shall not
exceed 48 months.
(End of Clause)

GENERAL INSTRUCTIONS FOR THE PREPARATION OF PROPOSAL
General rules for submission of a proposal to this solicitation are contained in MMAR 52.215-1, Instructions to Offerors-
Competitive Acquisition (Nov 2001).
a. Offerors are fully responsible for the accuracy, completeness, and compliance with all proposal instructions set
forth in the RFP. The penalty for making false statements to the Government is prescribed in 18 U.S.C. 1001
b. Section L provides instructions and other information related to the preparation of a proposal. Offerors are
cautioned to follow all instructions carefully to ensure the Government receives all requested information in a form
that will facilitate proposal evaluation.
Evaluation factors are contained in Section M. Failure to provide all required information may eliminate a proposal from
consideration or may make an offeror ineligible for award.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 28 of 35
C. The term "Offeror" as used in this solicitation refers to the single legal entity named in the Offer. The legal entity
must be a discrete entity separate from any other organization and may consist of the offeror team arrangement
with multiple team members. The Offeror is solely responsible for work performed under the contract resulting from
this solicitation.
d. If an Offeror does not follow the instructions set forth herein, the Government may determine an offer to be
unacceptable, or the Offeror's proposal may be eliminated from further consideration or the proposal may be
downgraded and not receive full or partial credit under the applicable evaluation criteria.
e. This solicitation does not commit the Government to pay any costs incurred in the submission of any offer
and other written and oral information, or in making necessary studies or designs for the preparation thereof or
to acquire contract for any services.
f. Any exceptions or deviations taken by the Offeror to the terms and conditions stated in this solicitation for
inclusion in the resulting contract may make the offer unacceptable for award without discussions.
g. It is the intent of the Government to award one contract as a result of this solicitation. The Government reserves
the right to make one or more awards based upon the number of acceptable proposals received and the
availability of funding.
h. If an Offeror does not understand the instructions in this solicitation, then it should write to the Contracting
Officer for clarification sufficiently in advance of the deadline for the receipt of proposals in order to obtain an
answer in time to meet that deadline.
i. Amendments to solicitations - If this solicitation is amended, all terms and conditions that are not amended
remain unchanged. Offerors shall acknowledge receipt of any amendment to this solicitation by the date and time
specified in the amendment(s).

General Instructions:
a. Instructions outlined in paragraph L.2 below prescribe the format for the proposal and describe the approach
for the development and presentation of proposal data. These instructions are designed to ensure the
submission of necessary information to provide for the understanding and comprehensive evaluation.
b. If an offeror believes that the requirements in these instructions contain an error, ambiguity, omission, or are
otherwise deemed unsound, the offeror shall immediately notify the Contracting Officer in writing with supporting
rationale. The offeror is reminded that the government reserves the right to award this requirement based on the
initial proposal, as received, without discussions.
L.2 Proposal Preparation Instructions:
The Offeror's complete proposal must be submitted in an Adobe PDF portfolio format. A PDF portfolio is a special type of
PDF file that acts as a container for multiple files of different formats. When the email comes in, we will only see one
portfolio file. Your portfolio shall consist of five (5) volumes titled as follows:
Volume 1: Signed SF 1449 and Company Information (to include any amendments)
Volume 2: Technical & Management Approach
Volume 3: Key Personnel
Volume 4: Past Performance
Volume 5: Cost/Price Proposal.
Proposal Content:
Volume 1: Signed SF 1449 and Company Information (and Amendments)
The offeror must sign and submit the Standard Form 1449 in this volume and the SF30 of any amendments. In
addition, the offeror must attach the following: 1) System for Award Management (SAM) registration
information, 2) a completed IRS Form W-9 Vendor Address and Taxpayer Identification Number (TIN), and 3)
identify a company point of contact, including the email address and phone number.
Volume 2: Technical & Management Approach
The offeror shall submit a detailed narrative that describes the company's corporate experience performing the
comprehensive scope of services outlined in the Statement of Work. The government will evaluate the offeror's
plan for organizing, staffing, and managing the contract with qualified personnel and the means that will be used
to accomplish the contract requirements. A Draft Quality Management Plan and Draft Schedule are required
and will be used to aid in evaluating the offeror's ability to maintain a high standard of work, especially in the
presence of obstacles. The proposal shall also identify typical challenges and describe practical methods for
identifying and mitigating risks.
Offerors must possess at least five (5) years of corporate experience providing relevant services in either the
commercial environment and/or in support of government agencies. Offerors must identify at least three
projects of similar complexity and provide a summary of work requirements, the dates of performance, the total
dollar value, and at least one point of contact.
Volume 3: Key Personnel
The offeror shall propose key personnel who possess the education, experience, and technical skills required to
perform their duties independently with minimal supervision, as outlined in the Statement of Work. The
government will evaluate the qualifications, experience, and capabilities of the proposed key personnel to
determine the extent to which they meet or exceed the requirements of the solicitation. The key personnel
specified below are considered essential to the work being performed under this contract. All personnel shall
possess the minimum education and experience identified in the table below. The government reserves the
right to interview all proposed key personnel, with the Contracting Officer notifying offerors of the date and time
for interviews. The offeror may put forward more key personnel not specified below.
The following positions are designated as key personnel for this contract:
Fire Pump Representative/Technician (1 FTE)
Sprinkler Technician (1 FTE)
Fire Alarm Technician (1 FTE)
Project Manager (1 FTE)

commercial customers that demonstrate recent and relevant past performance, scope, and complexity of this
requirement.

listed may be contacted for performance feedback.

must be referenced as cited under SECTION B- SUPPLIES/SERVICES AND PRICE. The total price proposed for
the base and option years of each CLIN, as outlined in Section B of this RFP, must be filled in and included in this
volume.

13. Section M - Evaluation Factors for Award
NOTICELISTING PROVISION CLAUSES INCORPORATED BY REFERENCE: The following
Contract clauses pertinent to this section are hereby incorporated by reference (by Citation Number, Title, and Date) in
accordance with the clause at MMAR 52.252-1 Solicitation Provisions Incorporated by Reference in Section M of this
Solicitation.
M.1 General Information
a. To be acceptable and eligible for evaluation, proposals must be prepared in accordance with Section L and must
meet all the requirements set forth in the other sections of this solicitation. The government will make an initial
review of proposals to determine compliance with these instructions. The government may determine an Offeror
to be unacceptable and exclude it from further consideration for failure to comply with Section L.
b. The Government may make award with our without discussions. Therefore, Offerors are advised to submit their
best technical and price proposals. When evaluating the competing Offerors, the government will consider the
written information provided by the Offerors and any other information obtained by the government through its own
research.
C. Evaluations focus on the information included in the proposal, resumes, experience, and the Offeror's past
performance review(s), and other information provided by the Offeror. The submitted technical information will be
evaluated by a technical evaluation committee using the technical acceptability criteria shown on the following
pages. The Government intends to conduct the evaluation and source selection process as detailed in Sections
M.2 and M.3. The Offerors must submit the proposal in response to this solicitation for all CLIN(s) listed in Section
B of this solicitation.
d. Award: The Government intends to award one contract resulting from this solicitation to the responsible
Offeror whose proposal represents the best value to the government. The government also reserves the right to
award more than one contract and/or not to award contract in response to this solicitation.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 32 of 35
M.2 Source Selection
a. The Government intends to evaluate Offerors in accordance with Section M of this RFP and make the contract
award to the responsible Offeror whose proposal represents the best value to the U.S. Government.
b. This procurement utilizes the Lowest Price Technically Acceptable (LPTA) process set forth in MMAR
15.101-2.
C. Responsibility Determination: The Contracting Officer will conduct a responsibility determination for the
successful offeror per MMAR Part 9.103.
M.3 Basis for Award
Award will be based on the lowest evaluated price of proposals meeting or exceeding the acceptability
standards for non-cost factors and sub-factors in accordance with MMAR Part 15.101-2 Lowest Price
Technically Acceptable (LPTA). The Government will assign an overall technical rating based on the
combined assessment of these factors.
The following technical factors will be rated against the acceptability criteria:
No.

M.4 The following evaluation criteria will be used to determine technical acceptability:
Rating
Technical Evaluation Definitions
Acceptable
Factor 1 - Technical & Management Approach
An Acceptable proposal demonstrates a thorough understand of the Statement of
Work, required resources, schedule, and other requirements essential to successful
contract performance. The offeror demonstrates at least five (5) years of corporate
experience by providing at least three (3) projects of similar complexity and provides
a summary of work requirements, dates of performance, total dollar value, and at
least one point of contact. The offeror provides a Draft Quality Management Plan
and Draft Schedule. The proposal demonstrates a technically sound management
approach that clearly defines the roles and responsibilities of key personnel, support
staff, and subcontractors, along with strategies for effective coordination, quality
assurance, and oversight.
Factor 2 - Key Personnel
Offeror provides key personnel who clearly possess the minimum experience and
credentials outlined and technical skills required to perform the assigned duties with
minimal supervision.
Factor 3 - Past Performance
GPO will evaluate the recency, relevancy, and quality of the offeror's past
performance as predictors of probably success under this requirement.
Acceptable proposals present a high probability of satisfying all requirements. Any
minor weaknesses identified can be readily corrected without significant government
oversight or risk to performance.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 33 of 35
Unacceptable
Factor 1 - Technical & Management Approach
Offeror's technical capability does not meet the Acceptable definition, is
incomplete, unrealistic, or demonstrates significant misunderstanding of the
Statement of Work and/or scope requirements. The offeror fails to demonstrate
the technical capability to satisfy contract performance. One or both of the
required Draft Quality Management Plan and Draft Schedule are not provided, or
the necessary corporate experience is not provided or detailed enough to meet the
definition of Acceptable.
Factor 2 - Key Personnel
The offeror's key personnel submission lacks the required experience,
qualifications, experience, technical expertise, or is missing from the proposal.
Factor 3 - Past Performance
Any past performance information provided is adverse and has not been responded
to, or past performance is not determined to be recent, relevant, or of appropriate
quality
Unacceptable proposals present a low probability of successful performance and
contain deficiencies or weaknesses that cannot be readily corrected without major
revisions.
M.5
Past Performance
The Government Publishing Office may obtain and consider past performance data from sources other than
those provided by the offeror, including existing federal database
GPO will evaluate the recency, relevancy, and quality of the offeror's past performance as predictors of
probable success under this requirement. Adverse past performance information, to which the offeror has not
previously responded, will be addressed IAW MMAR 15.3 procedures.
Recency: To be considered recent, projects must be ongoing or completed within the past six (6) years
from the date of solicitation issuance
Relevancy: Past performance will be assessed for similarity in size, scope, and complexity to this
solicitation. Both prime and any subcontractor experience may be considered
IAW MMAR 15.305(a)(2)(iv), an offeror's past performance will not be rated favorably or unfavorably when:
1. The offeror lacks relevant performance history; or
2. Performance information is unavailable
Offerors meeting these conditions will receive a neutral rating, though the Contracting Officer may consider a
broad range of available performance-related information prior to assigning such a rating.
M.6
Cost/Price Evaluation
Cost/Price Analysis Evaluation
The government will evaluate proposed prices to determine whether offers are complete, reasonable, and
realistic, and whether the proposed price reflects a clear understanding of the work requirements. The
evaluation will also assess consistency between the proposed price and the offeror's technical approach and
budget narrative.
040ADV-26-R-0021
Page 34 of 35
Fair and Reasonable Determination
Price evaluation will be conducted under the expectation of adequate price competition, relying primarily on
market forces to determine price reasonableness. Comparative analysis of proposed prices in response to this
solicitation will be the preferred method. GPO may also compare proposed prices to:
Historical prices for similar work; and
The Independent Government Cost Estimate (IGCE)
Additional techniques and procedures outlined in MMAR 15.404-1(b) may be employed, if necessary, to ensure
prices are fair and reasonable.
Responsiveness
No price evaluation will be performed on proposals determined to be non-responsive or technically

PART c - DESCRIPTION/SPECIFICATIONS
STATEMENT OF WORK (SOW)
ANNUAL PREVENTATIVE MAINTENANCE - FIRE SUPPRESSION AND FIRE ALARM
SYSTEMS
U.S. GOVERNMENT PUBLISHING OFFICE
1.0. GENERAL INFORMATION
1.1. Project Title
Annual Preventive Maintenance (PM) Services - Fire Suppression and Fire Alarm
Systems.
1.2. Contract Type
Firm-Fixed-Price (FFP) Service Contract.
1.3. Period of Performance
Base Year: One (1) year.
Option Years: Three (3) one-year options.
Total Contract Duration: Up to four (4) years.
Option years may be exercised at the sole direction of the Government.
1.4. Location
The United States Government Publishing Office (GPO) is located at 732 North
Capitol Street NW, Washington, DC 20401. The office produces and distributes
information products and services for all three branches of the Federal Government,
including U.S. passports for the Department of State as well as the official
publications of Congress, the White House, and other Federal agencies in digital and
print formats.
The existing fire suppression and fire alarm systems of the four GPO Buildings (A, B,
C, D) total a gross floor area of 1,419,507 square feet. A building list and system
inventory from the 2024 Annual PM Report will be provided as Government-
Furnished Information (GFI).
2.0. PROJECT OVERVIEW AND OBJECTIVES
The objective of this contract is to provide systematic, code-compliant preventive
maintenance, inspection, and testing of fire alarm and fire suppression systems to ensure:
Continuous life safety system operability.
Compliance with applicable codes and GPO standards.
Early identification of system deficiencies.
Accurate and complete system documentation.
3.0. SCOPE OF WORK
3.1. General Requirements
1
Annual PM - Fire Suppression & Fire Alarm Systems
U.S. Government Publishing Office
The Contractor shall furnish all labor, supervision, tools, equipment, materials,
documentation, and coordination necessary to perform annual preventive
maintenance services for the fire alarm and fire suppression systems in accordance
with this Statement of Work.
3.2. Systems Included
Services shall include inspection, testing, and reporting for the following systems,
where present:
Fire Suppression Systems:
Wet-pipe sprinkler systems
Dry-pipe and pre-action sprinkler systems.
Standpipe systems.
Fire pumps.
Control valves, supervisory devices, gauges, and alarms.
Fire Alarm Systems:
The buildings utilize EST3 systems manufactured by Edwards.
Fire alarm control panels (FACP).
Networked panels and remote annunciators.
Initiating devices (smoke, heat, duct detectors, manual pull stations).
Notification appliances (horns, strobes, speakers).
Power supplies, batteries, and circuit supervision.
Monitoring and communication interfaces.
3.3. Exclusions
The following are excluded from this contract unless separately authorized in writing
by the Contracting Officer:
Corrective repairs or system modifications.
Replacement of failed components.
System upgrades or code retrofit work.
Emergency response services.
4.0. APPLICABLE CODES, STANDARDS, AND CRITERIA
All services shall be performed in accordance with the latest adopted editions of the following:
Manufacturer requirements for EST3.
NFPA 13 - Installation of Sprinkler Systems (reference).
NFPA 14 - Installation of Standpipe Systems (reference).
NFPA 20 - Installation of Stationary Pumps for Fire Protection.
NFPA 25 - Inspection, Testing and Maintenance of Water Based Fire Protection
Systems.
NFPA 72 - National Fire Alarm and Signaling Code.
GPO Design Standards and Life Safety Requirements.
OSHA regulations and applicable Authority Having Jurisdiction (AHJ) requirements.
5.0. TECHNICAL REQUIREMENTS
2
Annual PM - Fire Suppression & Fire Alarm Systems
U.S. Government Publishing Office

The Contractor shall perform inspections and testing in accordance with NFPA 25,
including at a minimum:

Components Corrected After Deficiency Repair: The Contractor shall retest devices or circuits
repaired or replaced by Government personnel to verify proper operation. Retesting shall be
limited to affected components. All retests will be requested from the COR to the Contractor, and
will be priced under a separate, Not to Exceed (NTE) Contract Line-Item Number (CLIN). The
contractor shall respond to any retest requests within fourteen (14) calendar days.
5.2. Fire Alarm Annual Preventive Maintenance
The Contractor shall perform inspections and testing as required by NFPA 72 and
EST3 manufacturer requirements, including at a minimum:
FIRE ALARM INSPECTION AND TESTING REQUIREMENTS:
DEVICE
ANNUAL
Smoke detectors
TEST
Heat detectors
TEST
Pull stations
TEST
Duct smoke detectors
TEST
Waterflow switch
TEST
Dry pipe valves
TEST
Hi/Lo pressure switch
TEST
Tamper switch
TEST
Strobes/horns
TEST
Smoke detectors:
All detectors shall be tested with a listed spray test smoke.
All detectors shall be tested in all areas accessible to the Contractor.
A validation of all building interfaces shall be noted on the test report (HVAC shut-down,
elevator recall, etc.).
Heat detectors:
All restorable heat detectors shall be tested utilizing a heat gun (on low setting) or a hair
dryer.
Validation of all building interfaces shall be noted on test report (HVAC shut-down,
elevator recall, etc.).
Non-restorable heat detectors SHALL NOT be tested using a heat source.
Pull stations:
4
Annual PM - Fire Suppression & Fire Alarm Systems
U.S. Government Publishing Office
All pull stations shall be tested and re-set.
Validation of all building interfaces shall be noted on test report (HVAC shut-down,
elevator recall, etc.).
Duct smoke detectors: Provide testing as required by NFPA 72.
Waterflow switch: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25.
Dry pipe valves: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25.
Hi/Lo pressure switch: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25.
Tamper switch: Provide testing as required by NFPA 13 and 25. Switch shall give immediate
activation of supervisory signal at the fire alarm panel.
Strobes/horns: Provide testing as required by NFPA 72.
Tamper switch (for buildings equipped with sprinklers only): Each system valve tamper switch
shall be tested by partially closing the valve to initiate a tamper signal, locking in the nearby
monitor module.
Dry Valves (for buildings equipped with sprinklers only): Test pressure switch using the inspectors
test located on valve.
Alarm Devices:
All sprinkler alarm devices shall be serviced per the table. Verify alarm panel device
description/location for accuracy.
All sprinkler flow initiation devices shall alarm within 90 seconds.
System Checks:
No visible water leaks or standing water (clogged drains).
Record all test data, static pressures, residual pressures
Fire pump test shall not activate general alarm (denotes system pressure problems).
During weekly pump runs: verify fire pump and jockey pump start and stop pressures.
Jockey pump stop pressure shall be equal to or higher than fire pump churn (zero flow)
pressure. Jockey pump run cycles should be no more than 10 runs within a 24hr period.
Dry Sprinkler Valves:
All systems shall be drained for a minimum of 4 hours following a valve trip test.
Inspect for excessive compressor run.
Check for proper system air pressure per manufacturer's cut sheet.
Devices Corrected After Deficiency Repair: The Contractor shall retest devices or circuits
repaired or replaced by Government personnel to verify proper operation. Retesting shall be
limited to affected components.
6.0. SERVICE EXECUTION
6.1. Scheduling and Coordination
All work shall be coordinated with the GPO Contracting Officer's
Representative (COR).
Services shall be performed during normal business hours unless otherwise
approved.
5
Annual PM - Fire Suppression & Fire Alarm Systems
U.S. Government Publishing Office
Work shall be sequenced to minimized system downtime and occupant
disruption.
6.2. System Impairments
All impairments shall be coordinated and approved in advance.
Systems shall be fully restored to normal operation prior to Contractor
demobilization.
7.0. SUBMITTALS AND DELIVERABLES
7.1. Required Deliverables
For each building serviced, the Contractor shall submit:
Annual inspection and testing reports.
Device counts and test results.
Deficiency reports identifying:
Code deficiencies.
Non-code performance deficiencies.
Observed system conditions.
System status summary at completion.
Retest documentation for devices or components retested following
completion of deficiency repairs, including pass/fail results and confirmation
of system operation status.
7.2. Submittal Format and Timing
Reports shall be submitted electronically in PDF format.
Deliverables shall be submitted within ten (10) business days of service
completion for each building.
8.0. QUALITY ASSURANCE / QUALITY CONTROL (QA/QC)
The Contractor shall maintain a Quality Control Plan (QCP).
All work shall be performed by qualified, trained and properly certified technicians.
Fire Pump Representative/Technician:
Minimum of five (5) years of relevant work experience; and Qualified
and fire pump certified by the fire pump manufacturer for the fire
pump identified.
Sprinkler Technician:
Qualified to perform NFPA 25 inspection and testing.
Minimum of five (5) years of relevant work experience; and NICET
Inspection, Testing and Maintenance certified at Level Il or higher.
Fire Alarm Technician:
Qualified and experienced in accordance with Section 4.3.3. of
NFPA 72, National Fire Alarm Code, and NICET-certified at Level Il
or higher.
Minimum of five (5) years of experience servicing addressable fire
alarm systems.
Experience inspecting systems comparable in size/complexity to the
Government's EST3 systems.
6
Annual PM - Fire Suppression & Fire Alarm Systems
U.S. Government Publishing Office
No programming changes without Contracting Officer authorization.
The Government may witness inspections and testing at its discretion.
9.0. SAFETY AND SECURITY
The Contractor shall comply with all OSHA, GPO safety, and building security
requirements.
Personnel shall meet all badging and escort requirements.
Work areas shall be always maintained in a safe and orderly condition.
10.0. ACCEPTANCE AND VERIFICATION
Acceptance is contingent upon:
Completion of all required preventive maintenance tasks.
Restoration of systems to normal operational status.
Submission and Government acceptance of required documentation.
Incomplete or deficient work shall be corrected at no additional cost to the
Government.
Completion of required retesting following correction of identified deficiencies, where
applicable, and submission of corresponding retest documentation.
11.0. PROJECT MANAGEMENT AND COMMUNICATION
The Contractor shall designate a Project Manager as the single point of contact.
Project Manager Qualifications:
Minimum five (5) years of experience managing fire alarm and suppression
service contracts.
Experience managing multi-building facilities.
Familiarity with addressable fire alarm systems comparable to the
Government's EST3 systems.
Demonstrated knowledge of NFPA 72 and NFPA 25.
Issues affecting life safety or system operability shall be reported immediately to the
COR.
Coordination meetings shall be conducted as required.
12.0. CLOSEOUT
At the conclusion of the Base Year and each Option Year, the Contractor shall provide:
Final inspection and deficiency summary.
Confirmation of system operational status.
All outstanding documentation prior to final payment.
13.0. AGENCY OPERATIONS INFORMATION
13.1.
Hours of Service
The Contractor shall perform services during normal GPO business hours unless
otherwise directed by the Contracting Officer or Contracting Officer's Representative
(COR).
7
Annual PM - Fire Suppression & Fire Alarm Systems
U.S. Government Publishing Office
Normal Business Hours:
Monday through Friday, 7:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m.
After-Hours Work:
Certain tasks may require performance outside normal business hours,
including evenings, weekends, or Federal holidays, to support GPO
operations, emergency response, or to minimize disruption to occupants.
After-hours work shall be coordinated in advance with the COR.
No overtime, premium pay, or schedule changes shall be authorized unless
approved in advance by the COR.
13.2. Identification Badges and Security Access
All Contractor personnel requiring access to GPO facilities must comply with GPO
security and badging requirements. Contractor personnel shall obtain and visibly
display GPO-issued identification badges at all times while on GPO property. GPO
will provide affiliated badges with security background checks to the Contractor,
allowing them to escort their workers onto the premises. If a Contractor has not been
granted an affiliated badge, they must exchange a valid federal or state-issued
identification for a GPO Visitor's badge to enter the premises. Identification badges
are property of GPO and must be returned immediately upon contract completion,
personnel reassignment, or termination. Contractor personnel may be denied access
or have badges revoked for failure to comply with security policies or conduct
standards.
13.3. Sign-In / Sign-Out Requirements
All Contractor personnel are required to sign-in at 732 North Capitol St. NE
Washington, DC 22041. All Contractor personnel are required to sign-out at the same
location above.
13.4. Parking and Transportation
Parking within the GPO complex is extremely limited and not guaranteed. It is the
responsibility of Contractor personnel to purchase a parking pass for the designated
parking areas. GPO will not validate or make reimbursement for parking violations of
the Contractor's personnel under any circumstances. Unauthorized parking on GPO
property may result in citation, towing or revocation of site access privileges.
13.5. Conduct and Compliance
Contractor personnel shall conduct themselves in a professional manner consistent
with the operational environment of a Federal legislative complex. Smoking, tobacco
use, or e-cigarettes are prohibited inside all GPO buildings. No individual is permitted
to bring illegal drugs, alcohol or firearms of any type onto a government installation.
Disruptive behavior, failure to follow access procedures, or noncompliance with GPO
rules may result in removal from the site and replacement at no additional cost to the
Government.
13.6.
Contractor Responsibility
The Contractor shall be responsible all facilities in which the work will take place and
to also be familiar with the conditions under which the work will be accomplished. The
Contractor shall inspect existing conditions prior to commencing work, including
8
Annual PM - Fire Suppression & Fire Alarm Systems
U.S. Government Publishing Office
elements subject to damage or movement during the project. The Contractor shall
provide adequate personnel to reset alarm panels. Should the work create dust,
water or mud, the Contractor shall be responsible for cleaning the floors and walls.
The Contractor shall be responsible for the removal and replacement of all ceiling
tiles affected by the work.
13.7.
Tagging Requirements
The Contractor shall notify the COR/ACOR if panel alarm activation occurs
unexpectedly during inspection, testing and immediately upon occurrence. The
Contractor shall contact the COR/ACOR for procedures to take monitoring systems
offline during their procedures. The Contractor shall take all efforts to prevent this
from occurring with any regularity. A panel must show a "no fault or no trouble"
condition upon completion of test. After the tests and inspections are completed, the
Contractor shall contact the COR prior to placing monitoring systems back online,
and the appropriate tags will be attached indicating the system status. The Contractor
shall be responsible for any damage to the fire system during the work processes. If
applicable, the tagging and labeling system must clearly identify either a "blue"
(operational condition) or "yellow" (troubled condition but functional) or "red"
(Impaired or Fault but functional) or "red" (System Inoperable). This labeling system
applies to all circuit boards, components in the control panels, annunciator panels,
transponders, printers, keyboards, monitors, and peripheral devices (smoke
detectors, pull stations, audible and visible units, door contacts, tampers, flows, etc.)
associated with the fire alarm/sprinkler system.
